PlanPrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
The available knowledge is insufficient to assess the Claim. Therefore, **propose a set of actions** to retrieve new and helpful evidence. Adhere to the following rules:
* The actions available are listed under Valid Actions, including a short description for each action. No other actions are possible at this moment. 
* For each action, use the formatting as specified in Valid Actions.
* Include all actions in a single Markdown code block at the end of your answer.
* Propose as few actions as possible, but as much as needed. Do not propose similar or previously used actions.



## Valid Actions
* `geolocate`
   * Description: Performs geolocation to determine the country where an image was taken.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will determine the most likely countries where it was taken.
   * Format: geolocate(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `reverse_search`
   * Description: Performs a reverse image search to find similar images on the web.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will perform a reverse search to find similar images.
   * Format: reverse_search(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `image_search`
   * Description: Run an image search on Google to retrieve related images for a given query.
   * How to use: This is a helpful tool for fact-checking images. Use this to retrieve images associated with a specific keyword or phrase. Ensure that the query is clear and specific to improve search accuracy. If no relevant images are found, refine the query or use more descriptive terms.
   * Format: image_search("your image search query goes here")

# Example: geolocate()

## Claim
Text: "<image:k> shows a nuclear weapons facility in Usbekistan."

...

## Actions
```
geolocate(<image:k>)
```

# Example: reverse_search()

## Claim
Text: "<image:k> shows a rare event of a solar eclipse with a double ring."

...

## Actions
```
reverse_search(<image:k>)
```

# Example: image_search()

## Claim
Text: "Chinese officials in white protective hazmat suits carried people down a hallway to be quarantined for having COVID-19 in November 2022."

...

ACTIONS:
```
image_search("China officials white suits carry people")
image_search("China officials carry people COVID quarantine 2022")
```

# Record
## Claim
Claim: "President Donald Trump posted on Truth Social on July 25, 2024, as a reaction to the attempted assasination of him on July 13, 2024, 'I hope that America obliterates Israel.'"

# Your Actions



===== > RESPONSE:  < =====
```
image_search("Truth Social Donald Trump July 25 2024")
image_search("Donald Trump Truth Social Israel obliterate")
```

DevelopPrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
You just retrieved new Evidence. Now, **analyze the Claim's veracity using the evidence**. Always adhere to the following rules:
* Focus on developing new insights. Do not repeat larger parts from the Record. Do not restate the Claim.
* Write down your thoughts step-by-step. Whenever necessary, you may elaborate in more detail.
* Depending on the topic's complexity, invest one to three paragraphs. The fewer, the better.
* If you find that there is insufficient information to verify the Claim, explicitly state what information is missing.
* If you cite web sources, always refer to them by including their URL as a Markdown hyperlink.
* **Use information only from the recorded evidence**: Avoid inserting information that is not implied by the evidence. You may use commonsense knowledge, though.

# Record
## Claim
Claim: "President Donald Trump posted on Truth Social on July 25, 2024, as a reaction to the attempted assasination of him on July 13, 2024, 'I hope that America obliterates Israel.'"

## Actions
```
image_search("Truth Social Donald Trump July 25 2024")
image_search("Donald Trump Truth Social Israel obliterate")
```

## Evidence
### Evidence from `image_search`
The Los Angeles Times published an article on April 3, 2024, about Donald Trump's Truth Social activity, including an image of Donald Trump at the Bitcoin 2024 conference in Nashville, which took place from July 25-27, 2024 <image:7631>. The Guardian published an article about Donald Trump and Truth Social on May 20, 2024 <image:7632>.

*   [https://www.cnbc.com/video/2025/07/18/how-frequently-does-trump-post-on-social-media.html](https://www.cnbc.com/video/2025/07/18/how-frequently-does-trump-post-on-social-media.html)
*   [https://www.latimes.com/entertainment-arts/tv/story/2024-04-03/i-spent-24-hours-on-trump-truth-social-so-you-dont-have-to](https://www.latimes.com/entertainment-arts/tv/story/2024-04-03/i-spent-24-hours-on-trump-truth-social-so-you-dont-have-to)
*   [https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/article/2024/may/20/trump-truth-social-loss](https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/article/2024/may/20/trump-truth-social-loss)


### Evidence from `image_search`
NBC News ([https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/donald-trump/trump-engages-truth-social-diplomacy-iran-crisis-rcna214719](https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/donald-trump/trump-engages-truth-social-diplomacy-iran-crisis-rcna214719)) includes an image <image:7643> of a Truth Social post by Donald J. Trump, stating "THE CEASEFIRE IS NOW IN EFFECT. PLEASE DO NOT VIOLATE IT! DONALD J. TRUMP, PRESIDENT OF THE UNITED STATES!". The post was made 11 hours prior to the search.

Al Jazeera ([https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2025/6/25/12-posts-from-12-day-war-how-trump-live-posted-israel-iran-conflict](https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2025/6/25/12-posts-from-12-day-war-how-trump-live-posted-israel-iran-conflict)) published an article about Donald Trump's posts on Truth Social during a conflict between Iran and Israel, including posts from June 13 and June 15, 2025. <image:7644> The Atlantic ([https://www.theatlantic.com/politics/archive/2025/06/israel-iran-trump-truth-social/683306/](https://www.theatlantic.com/politics/archive/2025/06/israel-iran-trump-truth-social/683306/)) provides an image <image:7645> of a Truth Social post from Donald J. Trump, stating "ISRAEL is not going to attack Iran...". The post was made 4 hours prior to the publication of the article.


# Your Analysis



===== > RESPONSE:  < =====
The evidence confirms that Donald Trump uses Truth Social. The search results include articles about his activity on the platform, including posts related to international conflicts. However, there is no evidence in the provided documents to verify the specific claim about Trump's post on July 25, 2024, regarding Israel. The provided evidence includes posts from 2025, but not from the date mentioned in the claim.

To verify the claim, I would need to find a specific post from Donald Trump on Truth Social dated July 25, 2024, and containing the exact quote provided in the claim.

JudgePrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
**Determine the Claim's veracity** by following these steps:
1. Briefly summarize the key insights from the fact-check (see Record) in at most one paragraph.
2. Write one paragraph about which one of the Decision Options applies best. Include the most appropriate decision option at the end and enclose it in backticks like `this`.




## Decision Options
* `not enough information`: The fact-check does not contain sufficient information to come to an conclusion. For example,there is substantial lack of evidence or the evidence is inconclusive, conflicting or self-contradictory. In the case of a lack of evidence, state which information exactly is missing. In particular, if no RESULTS or sources are available, pick this decision.
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.
* `false`: The claim is not factually accurate. This is the case if one of the following three conditions is met:(1) The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources,(2) The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the origin, content and/or meaning of a statement or an image is misrepresented. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way,(3) There is not enough evidence to verify the claim or the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory.

# Record
## Claim
Claim: "President Donald Trump posted on Truth Social on July 25, 2024, as a reaction to the attempted assasination of him on July 13, 2024, 'I hope that America obliterates Israel.'"

## Actions
```
image_search("Truth Social Donald Trump July 25 2024")
image_search("Donald Trump Truth Social Israel obliterate")
```

## Evidence
### Evidence from `image_search`

PlanPrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
The available knowledge is insufficient to assess the Claim. Therefore, **propose a set of actions** to retrieve new and helpful evidence. Adhere to the following rules:
* The actions available are listed under Valid Actions, including a short description for each action. No other actions are possible at this moment. 
* For each action, use the formatting as specified in Valid Actions.
* Include all actions in a single Markdown code block at the end of your answer.
* Propose as few actions as possible, but as much as needed. Do not propose similar or previously used actions.



## Valid Actions
* `geolocate`
   * Description: Performs geolocation to determine the country where an image was taken.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will determine the most likely countries where it was taken.
   * Format: geolocate(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `reverse_search`
   * Description: Performs a reverse image search to find similar images on the web.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will perform a reverse search to find similar images.
   * Format: reverse_search(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `image_search`
   * Description: Run an image search on Google to retrieve related images for a given query.
   * How to use: This is a helpful tool for fact-checking images. Use this to retrieve images associated with a specific keyword or phrase. Ensure that the query is clear and specific to improve search accuracy. If no relevant images are found, refine the query or use more descriptive terms.
   * Format: image_search("your image search query goes here")

# Example: geolocate()

## Claim
Text: "<image:k> shows a nuclear weapons facility in Usbekistan."

...

## Actions
```
geolocate(<image:k>)
```

# Example: reverse_search()

## Claim
Text: "<image:k> shows a rare event of a solar eclipse with a double ring."

...

## Actions
```
reverse_search(<image:k>)
```

# Example: image_search()

# Instructions
You just retrieved new Evidence. Now, **analyze the Claim's veracity using the evidence**. Always adhere to the following rules:
* Focus on developing new insights. Do not repeat larger parts from the Record. Do not restate the Claim.
* Write down your thoughts step-by-step. Whenever necessary, you may elaborate in more detail.
* Depending on the topic's complexity, invest one to three paragraphs. The fewer, the better.
* If you find that there is insufficient information to verify the Claim, explicitly state what information is missing.
* If you cite web sources, always refer to them by including their URL as a Markdown hyperlink.
* **Use information only from the recorded evidence**: Avoid inserting information that is not implied by the evidence. You may use commonsense knowledge, though.

JudgePrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
**Determine the Claim's veracity** by following these steps:
1. Briefly summarize the key insights from the fact-check (see Record) in at most one paragraph.
2. Write one paragraph about which one of the Decision Options applies best. Include the most appropriate decision option at the end and enclose it in backticks like `this`.




## Decision Options
* `not enough information`: The fact-check does not contain sufficient information to come to an conclusion. For example,there is substantial lack of evidence or the evidence is inconclusive, conflicting or self-contradictory. In the case of a lack of evidence, state which information exactly is missing. In particular, if no RESULTS or sources are available, pick this decision.
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.
* `false`: The claim is not factually accurate. This is the case if one of the following three conditions is met:(1) The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources,(2) The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the origin, content and/or meaning of a statement or an image is misrepresented. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way,(3) There is not enough evidence to verify the claim or the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory.

PlanPrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
The available knowledge is insufficient to assess the Claim. Therefore, **propose a set of actions** to retrieve new and helpful evidence. Adhere to the following rules:
* The actions available are listed under Valid Actions, including a short description for each action. No other actions are possible at this moment. 
* For each action, use the formatting as specified in Valid Actions.
* Include all actions in a single Markdown code block at the end of your answer.
* Propose as few actions as possible, but as much as needed. Do not propose similar or previously used actions.



## Valid Actions
* `geolocate`
   * Description: Performs geolocation to determine the country where an image was taken.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will determine the most likely countries where it was taken.
   * Format: geolocate(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `reverse_search`
   * Description: Performs a reverse image search to find similar images on the web.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will perform a reverse search to find similar images.
   * Format: reverse_search(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `image_search`
   * Description: Run an image search on Google to retrieve related images for a given query.
   * How to use: This is a helpful tool for fact-checking images. Use this to retrieve images associated with a specific keyword or phrase. Ensure that the query is clear and specific to improve search accuracy. If no relevant images are found, refine the query or use more descriptive terms.
   * Format: image_search("your image search query goes here")

# Example: geolocate()

Text: "<image:k> shows a nuclear weapons facility in Usbekistan."

...

## Actions
```
geolocate(<image:k>)
```

```

SummarizeResultPrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
In order to find evidence that helps your fact-check, you just ran a web search which yielded a Search Result. **Your task right now is to summarize the Search Result.** What to include:
* information that might be useful for the fact-check (see Record)
* relevant images (refer to images by inserting their reference <image:k>)
* if available: the release date as well as the author or the publisher (e.g. the media company) of the search result.

Do NOT include:
* advertisements
* any other information not related to the Record or the Claim

Additional rules:
* Do not add any additional information besides the information in the Search Result.
* If the Search Result doesn't contain any relevant information for the fact-checking work, simply print one word in capital letters: "NONE".
* Keep your writing style like in the Examples 1, 2 and 3 provided to you.
* Try to filter out relevant information even if the search result is in a different language.

# Example 1
The search result from America Today provides several photographs of the Notre-Dame Cathedral fire on April 15, 2019. <image:i>, <image:j>, <image:k>. None of the images show the Eiffel Tower in the background.

NONE

* Focus on developing new insights. Do not repeat larger parts from the Record. Do not restate the Claim.

JudgePrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
**Determine the Claim's veracity** by following these steps:
1. Briefly summarize the key insights from the fact-check (see Record) in at most one paragraph.
2. Write one paragraph about which one of the Decision Options applies best. Include the most appropriate decision option at the end and enclose it in backticks like `this`.




## Decision Options
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.
* `false`: The claim is not factually accurate. This is the case if one of the following three conditions is met:(1) The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources,(2) The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the origin, content and/or meaning of a statement or an image is misrepresented. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way,(3) There is not enough evidence to verify the claim or the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory.

# Instructions
The available knowledge is insufficient to assess the Claim. Therefore, **propose a set of actions** to retrieve new and helpful evidence. Adhere to the following rules:
* The actions available are listed under Valid Actions, including a short description for each action. No other actions are possible at this moment. 
* For each action, use the formatting as specified in Valid Actions.
* Include all actions in a single Markdown code block at the end of your answer.
* Propose as few actions as possible, but as much as needed. Do not propose similar or previously used actions.



## Valid Actions
* `geolocate`
   * Description: Performs geolocation to determine the country where an image was taken.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will determine the most likely countries where it was taken.
   * Format: geolocate(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `reverse_search`
   * Description: Performs a reverse image search to find similar images on the web.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will perform a reverse search to find similar images.
   * Format: reverse_search(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `image_search`
   * Description: Run an image search on Google to retrieve related images for a given query.
   * How to use: This is a helpful tool for fact-checking images. Use this to retrieve images associated with a specific keyword or phrase. Ensure that the query is clear and specific to improve search accuracy. If no relevant images are found, refine the query or use more descriptive terms.
   * Format: image_search("your image search query goes here")

The articles can be found at the following URLs: [https://www.theguardian.com/world/2025/jan/18/a-visual-guide-to-the-destruction-of-gaza](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2025/jan/18/a-visual-guide-to-the-destruction-of-gaza), [https://www.npr.org/2024/10/09/g-s1-27175/israel-hamas-war-gaza-map](https://www.npr.org/2024/10/09/g-s1-27175/israel-hamas-war-gaza-map), and [https://www.aljazeera.com/gallery/2025/1/20/aerial-photos-show-scale-of-israeli-destruction-in-gaza](https://www.aljazeera.com/gallery/2025/1/20/aerial-photos-show-scale-of-israeli-destruction-in-gaza).


# Your Analysis



===== > RESPONSE:  < =====
The evidence suggests that the image is likely from the Middle East, with a high probability of being in Jordan or Palestine. However, the evidence does not confirm the exact date of the image.

Based on the evidence, the claim is likely true. However, the exact date of the image cannot be verified.

For example,there is substantial lack of evidence or the evidence is inconclusive, conflicting or self-contradictory. In the case of a lack of evidence, state which information exactly is missing. In particular, if no RESULTS or sources are available, pick this decision.
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.
* `false`: The claim is not factually accurate. This is the case if one of the following three conditions is met:(1) The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources,(2) The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the origin, content and/or meaning of a statement or an image is misrepresented. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way,(3) There is not enough evidence to verify the claim or the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory.

# Instructions
The available knowledge is insufficient to assess the Claim. Therefore, **propose a set of actions** to retrieve new and helpful evidence. Adhere to the following rules:
* The actions available are listed under Valid Actions, including a short description for each action. No other actions are possible at this moment.

* Include all actions in a single Markdown code block at the end of your answer.
* Propose as few actions as possible, but as much as needed. Do not propose similar or previously used actions.



## Valid Actions
* `geolocate`
   * Description: Performs geolocation to determine the country where an image was taken.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will determine the most likely countries where it was taken.
   * Format: geolocate(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `reverse_search`
   * Description: Performs a reverse image search to find similar images on the web.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will perform a reverse search to find similar images.
   * Format: reverse_search(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `image_search`
   * Description: Run an image search on Google to retrieve related images for a given query.
   * How to use: This is a helpful tool for fact-checking images. Use this to retrieve images associated with a specific keyword or phrase. Ensure that the query is clear and specific to improve search accuracy. If no relevant images are found, refine the query or use more descriptive terms.
   * Format: image_search("your image search query goes here")

# Record
## Claim

```

JudgePrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
**Determine the Claim's veracity** by following these steps:
1. Briefly summarize the key insights from the fact-check (see Record) in at most one paragraph.
2. Write one paragraph about which one of the Decision Options applies best. Include the most appropriate decision option at the end and enclose it in backticks like `this`.




## Decision Options
* `not enough information`: The fact-check does not contain sufficient information to come to an conclusion. For example,there is substantial lack of evidence or the evidence is inconclusive, conflicting or self-contradictory. In the case of a lack of evidence, state which information exactly is missing. In particular, if no RESULTS or sources are available, pick this decision.
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.
* `false`: The claim is not factually accurate. This is the case if one of the following three conditions is met:(1) The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources,(2) The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the origin, content and/or meaning of a statement or an image is misrepresented. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way,(3) There is not enough evidence to verify the claim or the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory.

# Record
## Claim
Claim: "Iran's IRGC Quds Force commander Gen. Esmail Qaani has fled Iran in April 2025 and is confirmed safe in Israel."

## Actions
```
image_search("Esmail Qaani Israel")
```

## Evidence
### Evidence from `image_search`
The search results include an image of a man in an Israeli military uniform with the Israeli flag in the background from [Source](https://www.theiranist.com/p/iran-attacks-israel-againand-more) <image:7704>. The Washington Institute provides an image of Esmail Qaani <image:7705>. The Times of Israel reports on claims about Esmail Qaani <image:7706>.


## Elaboration
The evidence includes an image of Esmail Qaani and an image of a man in an Israeli military uniform. The Times of Israel reports on claims about Esmail Qaani. However, there is no direct evidence confirming that Esmail Qaani has fled to Israel.

The search results do not provide any information about the date of April 2025.

Insufficient information is available to verify the claim.


# Your Judgement



===== > RESPONSE:  < =====
The search results show images of Esmail Qaani and a man in an Israeli military uniform, and mention claims about Qaani. However, there is no direct evidence confirming that Qaani has fled to Israel, nor is there any information about the date of April 2025.

`not enough information`

PlanPrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
The available knowledge is insufficient to assess the Claim. Therefore, **propose a set of actions** to retrieve new and helpful evidence. Adhere to the following rules:
* The actions available are listed under Valid Actions, including a short description for each action. No other actions are possible at this moment. 
* For each action, use the formatting as specified in Valid Actions.
* Include all actions in a single Markdown code block at the end of your answer.
* Propose as few actions as possible, but as much as needed. Do not propose similar or previously used actions.



## Valid Actions
* `geolocate`
   * Description: Performs geolocation to determine the country where an image was taken.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will determine the most likely countries where it was taken.
   * Format: geolocate(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `reverse_search`
   * Description: Performs a reverse image search to find similar images on the web.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will perform a reverse search to find similar images.
   * Format: reverse_search(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `image_search`
   * Description: Run an image search on Google to retrieve related images for a given query.
   * How to use: This is a helpful tool for fact-checking images. Use this to retrieve images associated with a specific keyword or phrase. Ensure that the query is clear and specific to improve search accuracy. If no relevant images are found, refine the query or use more descriptive terms.
   * Format: image_search("your image search query goes here")

# Example: geolocate()

## Claim
Text: "<image:k> shows a nuclear weapons facility in Usbekistan."

...

## Actions
```
geolocate(<image:k>)
```

# Example: reverse_search()

## Claim
Text: "<image:k> shows a rare event of a solar eclipse with a double ring."

...

## Actions
```
reverse_search(<image:k>)
```

# Example: image_search()

## Claim
Text: "Chinese officials in white protective hazmat suits carried people down a hallway to be quarantined for having COVID-19 in November 2022."

...

ACTIONS:
```
image_search("China officials white suits carry people")
image_search("China officials carry people COVID quarantine 2022")
```

JudgePrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
**Determine the Claim's veracity** by following these steps:
1. Briefly summarize the key insights from the fact-check (see Record) in at most one paragraph.
2. Write one paragraph about which one of the Decision Options applies best. Include the most appropriate decision option at the end and enclose it in backticks like `this`.




## Decision Options
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.
* `false`: The claim is not factually accurate. This is the case if one of the following three conditions is met:(1) The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources,(2) The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the origin, content and/or meaning of a statement or an image is misrepresented. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way,(3) There is not enough evidence to verify the claim or the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory.

## Valid Actions
* `geolocate`
   * Description: Performs geolocation to determine the country where an image was taken.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will determine the most likely countries where it was taken.
   * Format: geolocate(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `reverse_search`
   * Description: Performs a reverse image search to find similar images on the web.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will perform a reverse search to find similar images.
   * Format: reverse_search(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `image_search`
   * Description: Run an image search on Google to retrieve related images for a given query.
   * How to use: This is a helpful tool for fact-checking images. Use this to retrieve images associated with a specific keyword or phrase. Ensure that the query is clear and specific to improve search accuracy. If no relevant images are found, refine the query or use more descriptive terms.
   * Format: image_search("your image search query goes here")

JudgePrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
**Determine the Claim's veracity** by following these steps:
1. Briefly summarize the key insights from the fact-check (see Record) in at most one paragraph.
2. Write one paragraph about which one of the Decision Options applies best. Include the most appropriate decision option at the end and enclose it in backticks like `this`.




## Decision Options
* `not enough information`: The fact-check does not contain sufficient information to come to an conclusion. For example,there is substantial lack of evidence or the evidence is inconclusive, conflicting or self-contradictory. In the case of a lack of evidence, state which information exactly is missing. In particular, if no RESULTS or sources are available, pick this decision.
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.
* `false`: The claim is not factually accurate. This is the case if one of the following three conditions is met:(1) The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources,(2) The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the origin, content and/or meaning of a statement or an image is misrepresented. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way,(3) There is not enough evidence to verify the claim or the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory.

## Elaboration
The claim that the image shows a vegetable stand in Gaza with a Merkava tank is inaccurate. The reverse image search indicates that the image is from Syria, not Gaza. The tank in the image is not identified as a Merkava tank, and the evidence suggests it is an abandoned tank used as a fruit and vegetable stand in Syria.


# Your Judgement



===== > RESPONSE:  < =====
The image is not from Gaza, but from Syria. The tank is not identified as a Merkava tank. The claim misrepresents the location and the type of tank.

`false`

Penny Wong urges Israel to end Rafah offensive as Israeli forces reportedly reach city's centre

*   [Topic:Unrest, Conflict and War](/news/topic/unrest-conflict-and-war)
    

Tue 28 May 2024Tuesday 28 May 2024Tue 28 May 2024 at 10:23am

Israel has pounded Rafah with air strikes and tank fire, pressing its offensive in the southern Gaza city despite international condemnation of an attack that sparked a blaze in a tent camp for the displaced, [killing at least 45 people](/news/2024-05-27/israel-military-prosecutor-says-rafah-strike-under-investigation/103899588)
.

Reacting to Sunday night's strike and fire in a camp where thousands of displaced families from elsewhere in the Gaza Strip had sought shelter, global leaders urged the implementation of a World Court order to halt Israel's assault.

Israeli military spokesman Rear Admiral Daniel Hagari said on Tuesday the military had fired two 17-kilogram munitions in the strike that targeted two senior Hamas militants.

He said the munitions would have been too small to ignite a fire on their own, and the army was looking into the possibility that weapons were stored in the area.

Foreign Minister Penny Wong said the air strikes on Rafah showed why an immediate humanitarian ceasefire was needed.

She said Australia had been very clear that Israel must not proceed with its operation there.

"The death and destruction in Rafah is horrific. This human suffering is unacceptable," Senator Wong said, speaking at Senate estimates on Tuesday.

"We reiterate to the government of Israel: This cannot continue.

"We must see an immediate humanitarian ceasefire so civilians can be protected and Australia continues to support the work of the United States, Qatar and Egypt to that end.

"We continue to call for the release of all hostages by Hamas and for Israel to allow aid to flow at scale, as directed by the International Court of Justice."

Loading Twitter content

Several Israeli tanks on Tuesday reached the centre of Rafah, witnesses told Reuters, three weeks into a ground operation in the southern Gaza Strip city that has has drawn intense scrutiny from neighbouring Egypt and from the United States.

The tanks were spotted near Al-Awda mosque, a central Rafah landmark, the witnesses said. The Israeli military did not immediately comment on their account, saying it would issue a statement about the Rafah operation later.

!A man, woman and three young children walk down a street carrying bags and backpacks, youngest child sits in a pram <image:2102>

One million Palestinians have fled from Rafah in the past three weeks, UNRWA says. (Reuters: Hatem Khaled)

At least 16 Palestinians were killed in strikes overnight on Tuesday, officials in the enclave run by Hamas militants said. Israeli tanks pushed towards western neighbourhoods in one of the worst nights of bombardment reported by residents to news agency Reuters.

Before the latest advancement, Israeli tanks had probed around the edges of Rafah, near the crossing point from Gaza into Egypt, and entered some of its eastern districts, residents said, but had not yet entered the city in full force.

Residents said Israeli tanks were stationed on and around the Zurub hilltop, a high ground overlooking western Rafah, having advanced from the area near the Egyptian border crossing where Israeli forces launched an incursion three weeks ago.

They said the Tel Al-Sultan area, the scene of Sunday's deadly strike, was still being heavily bombarded.

"Tank shells are falling everywhere in Tel Al-Sultan. Many families have fled their houses in western Rafah under fire throughout the night," one resident told Reuters over a chat app.

One million have fled Rafah in past three weeks, UNRWA says
-----------------------------------------------------------

Around one million people have fled the Israeli offensive in Rafah since early May, the UN agency for Palestinian refugees (UNRWA) said on Tuesday.

Israel has kept up attacks despite [a ruling by the top UN court](/news/2024-05-24/un-top-court-orders-israel-to-half-rafah-offensive/103892078)
 on Friday ordering it to stop, arguing the court's ruling grants it some scope for military action there.

!Several smoke clouds rise over an urban landscape with multi-storey concrete buildings <image:2104>

Smoke rises over Rafah following Israeli strikes. (Reuters: Hatem Khaled)

More than 36,000 Palestinians have been killed in Israel's offensive, according to Gaza's health ministry.

Israel launched the operation after Hamas-led militants attacked southern Israeli communities on October 7, killing around 1,200 people and seizing more than 250 hostages, according to Israeli tallies.

Israel says it wants to root out Hamas fighters holed up in Rafah and rescue hostages it says are being held in the area.

In Jabalia in the northern Gaza Strip, one of the largest of the enclave's eight historic refugee camps, Israeli forces have been engaged in fierce fighting with Hamas and Islamic Jihad fighters, residents said.

On Tuesday, medics said an Israeli air strike killed and wounded several Palestinians in a house in the Falouja neighbourhood. Civil emergency teams said they believed many bodies were under the rubble of buildings where they can't be reached.

Spain, Norway, Ireland recognise Palestinian state
--------------------------------------------------

Spain, Ireland and Norway officially recognised a Palestinian state on Tuesday, despite an angry reaction from Israel, which has found itself increasingly isolated after more than seven months of conflict in Gaza.

Madrid, Dublin and Oslo said they sought to accelerate efforts to secure a ceasefire and hoped their decision would spur other European Union countries to follow suit.

"It's the only way of advancing toward what everyone recognises as the only possible solution to achieve a peaceful future, one of a Palestinian state that lives side by side with the Israeli state in peace and security," Spanish Prime Minister Pedro Sanchez said in a televised address.

Spain was recognising a unified Palestinian state, including the Gaza Strip and the West Bank, under the Palestinian National Authority with East Jerusalem as its capital, he said.

The Palestinian Authority, which exercises limited self-rule in the West Bank under Israeli military occupation, has welcomed the decision.

Ireland's Department of Foreign Affairs said last week it would upgrade its representative office in Ramallah in the West Bank to an embassy and appoint an ambassador and upgrade the status of the Palestinian mission in Ireland to an embassy.

Norway had until recently followed the position of the United States, which insists that a two-state solution can only be achieved through dialogue, but lost confidence that this strategy would work.

"In the middle of a war, with tens of thousands of dead and injured, we must keep alive the only thing that can provide a safe home for both Israelis and Palestinians: two states that can live in peace with each other," Norwegian Prime Minister Jonas Gahr Stre said last week.

Israel has repeatedly condemned the move and said it bolsters Hamas.

"Sanchez, when you  recognise a Palestinian state, you are complicit in incitement to genocide against the Jewish people and in war crimes," Israeli Foreign Minister Israel Katz wrote on X on Tuesday.

Denmark's parliament on Tuesday voted down a bill to recognise a Palestinian state, after the Danish foreign minister previously said the necessary preconditions for an independent country were lacking.

# Search Result
From [Source](https://globalaffairs.org/commentary-and-analysis/blogs/russian-youth-more-favorable-toward-israel-older-generations): Found exact image on website with title: Russian Youth More Favorable Toward Israel than Older Generations
Content: "[Skip to main content](#main-content)

Ohad Zwigenberg / AP

![Israeli tanks head towards the Gaza Strip border](/themes/custom/ccga/frontend/static-html/images/placeholder.png)

Young Russians may be more likely than their elders to give Israel the benefit of the doubt in its conflict with Hamas.

Introduction
------------

Unlike most Western and Western-aligned countries, Israel refused to [sanction or cut ties](https://carnegieendowment.org/russia-eurasia/politika/2023/11/israel-and-russia-the-end-of-a-friendship?lang=en)
 with Russia after it invaded Ukraine in 2022 and has since [maintained its neutrality](https://www.cfr.org/article/why-israel-has-been-slow-support-ukraine)
 in the conflict. At the time, Israeli Prime Minister Benjamin Netanyahu and Russian President Vladimir Putin had a [close personal relationship](https://carnegieendowment.org/russia-eurasia/politika/2023/11/israel-and-russia-the-end-of-a-friendship?lang=en)
 that had sustained warm relations between their countries for over a decade. However, their relationship cooled in 2023, as Russia and Iran began to develop a[major bilateral agreement](https://www.iranintl.com/en/202501046766)
 to expand their military, economic, and political cooperation that was [signed just last week](https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2025/1/17/russia-and-iran-presidents-sign-partnership-treaty-in-moscow)
.

Relations between Israel and Russia further deteriorated in the aftermath of Hamas October 7, 2023, attack against Israel. Putin refused to designate the group as a terrorist organization and instead invited a delegation from Hamas to Moscow for peace talks, calling for a [two-state solution](https://www.reuters.com/world/putin-tells-abbas-great-pain-palestinian-plight-2024-08-13/)
 to the longstanding conflict.

Data from a joint Chicago Council on Global Affairs and Levada Analytical Center survey, fielded September 26-October 2, 2024, finds that most Russians share Putins view of the conflict and believe Israeli military operations in Gaza are unjustified. However, the data reveal some differences in attitudes toward the war between young Russians and those from older generations.

Young Russians are Less Critical of Israeli Military Operations in Gaza
-----------------------------------------------------------------------

Despite the Kremlins diplomatic support for the Palestinian people, most Russians do not side with either party in the Israeli-Palestinian conflict (57%). However, among those who do choose a side, more side with Palestinians (28%) than with Israelis (6%). Young Russians are more likely to say they want to remain neutral in the conflict than older generations, who, by comparison, are less likely to be impartial and much more likely to side with Palestinians. Less than two in 10 Russians between 18-34 (14%) place themselves on the side of Palestinians, compared to four in 10 of the oldest cohort (40%).

Russian youth also have different opinions on Israels military operations in Gaza since the October 7, 2023, attack. Most Russians (59%) believe Israel has gone too far and its military actions are not justified, but young Russians are the least likely to say so (45%). In fact, they are nearly 30 percentage points less likely to say Israel has gone too far than the oldest cohort of Russians (70%). By contrast, they are the age group most likely to say Israel is justified and defending its interests (22%) or decline to answer the question entirely (33%).

. and View Israel and the United States More Favorably
-------------------------------------------------------

As the United States closest ally in the Middle East, Israel is likely perceived by Russians as being aligned with the West and is, as a result, viewed unfavorably by much of the population. Half of Russians express a negative view of Israel (51%), while less than a third (27%) say they feel very or somewhat good about the country.

Young Russians are divided in their views of Israel, as nearly as many express a negative opinion (37%) as express a positive one (42%). However, they are much more likely than older Russiansmajorities of whom express a negative viewto say they feel positively about Israel.

In the same vein, Russian youth are more likely to think Israel plays a positive role in resolving the key challenges facing the Middle East (23%) than other age groups, though nearly half (48%) contend that the country plays a negative role in the region. On this they differ from most Russians overall, who believe Israel plays a negative role in resolving regional challenges (60%), second only to the United States (71% negative role), which is viewed the most negatively. On the other hand, the majority of Russians (82%) believe their own country plays the most positive role in the region, followed by Iran (43%).

Russian youth also place less blame on the United States or Israel for the continued bloodshed and instability faced by the Middle East than do older Russians. Young Russians are the least likely to say that Israel (16%) or the United States and other Western countries (30%) are responsible for the conflict in the Middle East and are the most likely to place blame on Hamas and the Palestinians (12%) or no one in particular (16%).

Among the broader population, most consider the United States and other Western countries most responsible for the continued bloodshed and instability in the Middle East (38%)even more than Israel (22%) or Hamas (8%).

Social Media Contributes to Young Russians Alternative Views
-------------------------------------------------------------

Overall, pluralities of both Russian youth and older generations do not side with either party in the conflict, believe Israeli military operations in Gaza have gone too far, and blame the United States and other Western countries for the continued bloodshed in the region. However, younger Russians do so to a lesser extent than their elders and view Israel, the United States, and the West through a relatively more positive lens.

Why might this be? A [February 2024 Chicago Council-Levada Center survey](https://globalaffairs.org/research/public-opinion-survey/young-russians-are-skeptical-most-media-outlets)
 of just the youth population finds that they primarily receive their news and information about the world from digital media sources, like social media platforms, Telegram channels, and blogs. Unlike older generations, who most often turn to traditional, state-controlled media outlets like television, radio, and newspapers for their news, young Russians are exposed to more diverse sources of information online that are less censored and restricted by the Russian government. As a result, their political sentiments and views of Russian foreign policies differ from those of older generations, who are more likely to accept state narratives that are propagated through traditional media outlets.

Conclusion
----------

Despite the fall of Bashar al-Assads regime in Syria and Russias withdrawal from the country, Putins diplomatic support for the Palestinians, Hamas, and Iran has helped to counter Western influence in the Middle East and emphasize Russias role in the region. While young Russians share Putins anti-Western outlook on the conflict, they may be more likely to give Israel the benefit of the doubt than older generations of Russians.

Generational differences in views toward the Israel-Gaza war may exist as a result of the youth populations exposure to diverse narratives and sources of information online. In the current atmosphere that squelches dissent or protest in Russia, it is possible that young Russians may be projecting their position on their own countrys war in Ukraine onto their views of the war in the Middle East. Russian youth are far less likely than their elders to [personally support the military operation in Ukraine](https://globalaffairs.org/research/public-opinion-survey/young-russians-feel-more-threatened-terrorism-war-ukraine)
 and could be voicing some opposition to the states official narratives about both conflicts.

JudgePrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
**Determine the Claim's veracity** by following these steps:
1. Briefly summarize the key insights from the fact-check (see Record) in at most one paragraph.
2. Write one paragraph about which one of the Decision Options applies best. Include the most appropriate decision option at the end and enclose it in backticks like `this`.




## Decision Options
* `not enough information`: The fact-check does not contain sufficient information to come to an conclusion. For example,there is substantial lack of evidence or the evidence is inconclusive, conflicting or self-contradictory. In the case of a lack of evidence, state which information exactly is missing. In particular, if no RESULTS or sources are available, pick this decision.
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.
* `false`: The claim is not factually accurate. This is the case if one of the following three conditions is met:(1) The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources,(2) The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the origin, content and/or meaning of a statement or an image is misrepresented. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way,(3) There is not enough evidence to verify the claim or the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory.

PlanPrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
The available knowledge is insufficient to assess the Claim. Therefore, **propose a set of actions** to retrieve new and helpful evidence. Adhere to the following rules:
* The actions available are listed under Valid Actions, including a short description for each action. No other actions are possible at this moment. 
* For each action, use the formatting as specified in Valid Actions.
* Include all actions in a single Markdown code block at the end of your answer.
* Propose as few actions as possible, but as much as needed. Do not propose similar or previously used actions.



## Valid Actions
* `geolocate`
   * Description: Performs geolocation to determine the country where an image was taken.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will determine the most likely countries where it was taken.
   * Format: geolocate(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `reverse_search`
   * Description: Performs a reverse image search to find similar images on the web.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will perform a reverse search to find similar images.
   * Format: reverse_search(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `image_search`
   * Description: Run an image search on Google to retrieve related images for a given query.
   * How to use: This is a helpful tool for fact-checking images. Use this to retrieve images associated with a specific keyword or phrase. Ensure that the query is clear and specific to improve search accuracy. If no relevant images are found, refine the query or use more descriptive terms.
   * Format: image_search("your image search query goes here")

JudgePrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
**Determine the Claim's veracity** by following these steps:
1. Briefly summarize the key insights from the fact-check (see Record) in at most one paragraph.
2. Write one paragraph about which one of the Decision Options applies best. Include the most appropriate decision option at the end and enclose it in backticks like `this`.




## Decision Options
* `not enough information`: The fact-check does not contain sufficient information to come to an conclusion. For example,there is substantial lack of evidence or the evidence is inconclusive, conflicting or self-contradictory. In the case of a lack of evidence, state which information exactly is missing. In particular, if no RESULTS or sources are available, pick this decision.
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.
* `false`: The claim is not factually accurate. This is the case if one of the following three conditions is met:(1) The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources,(2) The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the origin, content and/or meaning of a statement or an image is misrepresented. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way,(3) There is not enough evidence to verify the claim or the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory.

PlanPrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
The available knowledge is insufficient to assess the Claim. Therefore, **propose a set of actions** to retrieve new and helpful evidence. Adhere to the following rules:
* The actions available are listed under Valid Actions, including a short description for each action. No other actions are possible at this moment. 
* For each action, use the formatting as specified in Valid Actions.
* Include all actions in a single Markdown code block at the end of your answer.
* Propose as few actions as possible, but as much as needed. Do not propose similar or previously used actions.



## Valid Actions
* `geolocate`
   * Description: Performs geolocation to determine the country where an image was taken.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will determine the most likely countries where it was taken.
   * Format: geolocate(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `image_search`
   * Description: Run an image search on Google to retrieve related images for a given query.
   * How to use: This is a helpful tool for fact-checking images. Use this to retrieve images associated with a specific keyword or phrase. Ensure that the query is clear and specific to improve search accuracy. If no relevant images are found, refine the query or use more descriptive terms.
   * Format: image_search("your image search query goes here")

# Example: geolocate()

```

```

JudgePrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
**Determine the Claim's veracity** by following these steps:
1. Briefly summarize the key insights from the fact-check (see Record) in at most one paragraph.
2. Write one paragraph about which one of the Decision Options applies best. Include the most appropriate decision option at the end and enclose it in backticks like `this`.




## Decision Options
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.
* `false`: The claim is not factually accurate. This is the case if one of the following three conditions is met:(1) The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources,(2) The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the origin, content and/or meaning of a statement or an image is misrepresented. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way,(3) There is not enough evidence to verify the claim or the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory.

# Instructions
The available knowledge is insufficient to assess the Claim. Therefore, **propose a set of actions** to retrieve new and helpful evidence. Adhere to the following rules:
* The actions available are listed under Valid Actions, including a short description for each action. No other actions are possible at this moment. 
* For each action, use the formatting as specified in Valid Actions.
* Include all actions in a single Markdown code block at the end of your answer.
* Propose as few actions as possible, but as much as needed. Do not propose similar or previously used actions.



## Valid Actions
* `geolocate`
   * Description: Performs geolocation to determine the country where an image was taken.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will determine the most likely countries where it was taken.
   * Format: geolocate(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `reverse_search`
   * Description: Performs a reverse image search to find similar images on the web.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will perform a reverse search to find similar images.
   * Format: reverse_search(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `image_search`
   * Description: Run an image search on Google to retrieve related images for a given query.
   * How to use: This is a helpful tool for fact-checking images. Use this to retrieve images associated with a specific keyword or phrase. Ensure that the query is clear and specific to improve search accuracy. If no relevant images are found, refine the query or use more descriptive terms.
   * Format: image_search("your image search query goes here")

Since the past weekend, Israel and Hezbollah have engaged in the [most intense exchange of fire](/en/middle-east-idf-prepares-for-possibility-of-lebanon-entry/live-70318800)
 one year into the Israel-Hamas warin [Gaza](/en/gaza/t-19074241)
. The armed wing of the Iran-backed Shiite political party and militant group, which is considered a terrorist organization by the US, Germany and several Sunni Arab countries,fired projectiles deeper into Israeli territory than ever before.

On Saturday, Israel launched waves of strikes against Hezbollah targets, describing the action as preemptive to thwart a planned attack. .

Lebanon's Health Ministry reported at least 569people killed, including 50children, and more than 1,800 wounded since Monday.

The recent escalation between [Israel](/en/israel/t-19067044)
 and [Hezbollah](/en/hezbollah/t-41508807)
 has also fueled a surge of misleading content. A recurrent theme in social media posts involves manipulated visuals claiming to show Hezbollah's attacks on Israel. Often out of context or entirely unrelated, these videos have gone viral on social media platforms. [DW Fact check](/en/fact-check/t-56584214)
investigatedsome of these viral claims.

Does this image show the aftermath of a Hezbollah attack on Ramat David airbase?
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Claim:** "_Despite Israel's hermetic military censorship. A photograph was leaked of the Ramat David base, which was attacked by Hezbollah at dawn today. Israel does not acknowledge that anything has happened at this air base,_" reads[the caption of a viral image](https://archive.is/uwdRN "External link  the caption of a viral image")
 circulating on social media. The image shows a large aircraft engulfed in flames, surrounded by vehicles at an airport, with military trucks and personnel scattered in the scene.

The Hezbollah attack targeted the Ramat David airbase near Haifa on Sunday, but this picture is fakeImage: Reddit

The image has been shared across multiple platforms, including[X](https://ghostarchive.org/archive/OH9Ef "External link  X")
 (formerly Twitter), [Reddit](https://archive.is/uwdRN "External link  Reddit")
, and [Threads](https://ghostarchive.org/archive/wjvSK "External link  Threads")
, reaching users in several languages, including Arabic.

**DW Fact check:** Fake.

Israeli media have[reported](https://www.jpost.com/israel-news/article-821267 "External link  reported")
 on the attack at Ramat David airbase in the North of the country, which occurred on Sunday morning. However, there are clear indications that the image being shared is AI-generated.

One of the most prominent signs of this being AI-generated content is the blurry andindecipherable text. The vehicle in the middle, closer to the camera, shows what appears to be writing on its side, but the text is distorted and unreadable. Some characters resemble Hebrew letters, but others don't make any sense. This is a common AI flaw, known as a "hallucination," which occurs when the system creates elements that don't exist or don't make sense in the real world.

Some details in the image are distorted, unrealistic or blurred which are indicators of it being AI-generatedImage: Reddit

The image also shows multiple visual distortions, particularly in the shapes and outlines of objects. The truck in the foreground has an awkward curve in its loading section. The vehicles closest to the plane seem fused, with their outlines merging unnaturally, making them difficult to distinguish. Most military vehicles in the image look unrealistic. Such errors are typical in AI-generated images.

Also, the aircraft's wing appears misaligned, and its body has anodd bump. Even more telling is the unrealistic clarity of the flames in the image, which contrasts withthe somewhat blurry and distorted vehicles and other surrounding details.

The inconsistencies strongly indicate that the image is AI-generated rather than an authentic photograph of a realattack on the Ramat David airbase.

DW Fact check conducted an analysis using Truemedia, a nonprofit tool specialized in detecting political deepfakes on social media. The tool's digital analysis uncovered substantial signs of manipulation, which the platformlater corroborated by human experts.

An analysis by Truemedia, a tool that detects digitally manipulated images, indicates that the image is most likely AI-generated.Image: Screenshot truemedia.org

Footage of fireworks in Algeria and fire in Indonesia claimed to show Israel under attack
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Claim:** A viral [post](https://ghostarchive.org/archive/x9SDs "External link  post")
 shared on September 22 reads, "_Hezbollah turned Israel to Isra-Hell_,"accompanied by a minute-long video. The video is a compilation of several unrelated clips, with sounds of gunfire, sirens, and screaming added throughout the video to create a sense of continuity. The first few secondsshowglowing lights illuminating the night sky in a public space, while the second part depicts scenes of chaos, with areas engulfed in flames at night.

The post has been widely circulated in multiple languages, including[English](https://archive.is/gvqGS "External link  English")
, [Arabic](https://ghostarchive.org/archive/bxOb7 "External link  Arabic")
, [Urdu](https://archive.ph/omoFJ "External link  Urdu")
and [Hindi,](https://ghostarchive.org/archive/Amha5 "External link  Hindi,")
all suggesting the video shows the aftermath of a Hezbollah missile attack on Israel.

A quick search of a screenshot from the video reveals it is old and unrelated to the current tensions. In many cases, fake videos and misinformation can be debunked through a reverse image search.Image: X

**DW Fact check:** False.

A reverse image search of a screenshot from the first part of the clipreveals that the video is not from the recent conflict. It originates from Algeria and shows the [celebrations of the 103rd anniversary](https://archive.is/B6E0I "External link  celebrations of the 103rd anniversary")
 of the Mouloud d'Alger soccer club  not military action.

There are [more videos](https://ghostarchive.org/varchive/vFs3bALRF1 "External link  more videos")
 of the same event online, which show the police officers in uniforms labeled "G.I.P,"consistent with those of [Algerian law enforcement.](https://archive.ph/VtzUB "External link  Algerian law enforcement.")
And these celebrations took placeat the beginning of August.

The same applies to other parts of the clips.They are also unrelated to the current conflict between Hezbollah and Israel and have been circulating for at least two years, [previously claiming](https://ghostarchive.org/archive/rD9EW "External link  previously claiming")
 to [show a fire](https://ghostarchive.org/archive/06ytm "External link  show a fire")
 in an Indonesian rural area.

DW could not verify the exact locations where the videos were filmed. However, the fact that the clips are at least two years old confirms they have no connection to the ongoing hostilities.

Some clips have been mirrored from original versions, making reverse image searches more difficult and complicating efforts to track down the original sources of the images.

We were unable to track down prior publications for one segment of the clip.

Footage of Russian oil refinery attack misrepresented as Hezbollah drone strike
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Claim:** "_Hezbollah drones reached the oil refineries in the north of occupied Palestine_,"claims a [post on X](https://archive.ph/qP3YN "External link  post on X")
. Hezbollah and other anti-Israeli groups refer to Israel as "occupied Palestine"because they do not recognize it as a legitimate country.Attached to the post is a video purportedly showing a drone flying over an industrial site, striking part of the facility, and exploding. The footage has been shared by numerous accounts on X with similar claims.

This footage has been verified to show a Ukrainian drone strike on a Russian oil refinery in July 2024Image: X

**DW Fact check:** False.

A reverse image search of a screenshot from the video reveals it dates back to the end of July. The footage actually shows a [Ukrainian drone attack on an oil refinery in Tuapse](https://www.youtube.com/shorts/a5NSXybWbWk "External link  Ukrainian drone attack on an oil refinery in Tuapse")
, located in the Krasnodar region of Russia, approximately two months ago.

This is a view of the oil refinery in Tuapse in 2020, with storage tanks and a valley shape matching the location seen in the video.Image: Igor Onuchin/TASS/imago

Hezbollah [has claimed](https://archive.ph/r9iC5 "External link  has claimed")
 it targeted several Israeli military installations on Tuesday, including an explosives factory 60 kilometers (37 miles) into Israel.

The militant group also reportedly launched a ballistic missile at Tel Aviv. While the Israeli military intercepted the surface-to-surface missile, there were no reports of casualties or damage. This marked the first time a projectile fired from Lebanon had reached central Israel, according to the Israeli military.

However, many images circulating online that claim to show the aftermath of these attacks are fake.

_Emad Hassan and TilmanWagner contributed to this report._

Hvordan oppdage falskt innhold?
-------------------------------

Hvis du stiller deg selv de riktige sprsmlene, er det mindre sannsynlig at du blir et offer for manipulerte bilder og historier.

Hvem er kilden?

Undersk hvem avsenderen er. Se hva annet kilden deler, og sjekk om vedkommende vil st ved informasjonen med navn og ansikt.

Hvorfor ble materialet delt?

Manipulert materiale er ofte designet for  skape en flelsesmessig respons og for  spille p folks fordommer.

Er det tegn p AI?

Bilder generert av kunstig intelligens kan fortsatt ofte avslres ved  zoome inn p detaljer. Noen ganger mangler detaljer som fingre og tr, eller det er for mange.

Stemmer datoen?

Ser du egentlig p et gammelt innlegg? Sjekk om vret, rstid og tid p dgnet stemmer overens med hendelsen som avsender sier bildet er fra.

Hvem delte den frst?

Bruk et bildeskeprogram som Google Lens for  finne ut om andre ogs deler bildet og i hvilken sammenheng det deles.

Den delagte basen
------------------

  ![KI-BILDE: Bildet her ble delt 23. september 2024, etter at Hizbollah utfrte et rakettangrep mot Israel. Foto: X / @drhossamsamy65](https://www.cdn.tv2.no/images/17063718.webp?imageId=17063718&x=0.00&y=0.00&cropw=100.00&croph=100.00&width=675&height=743 "Foto: X / @drhossamsamy65")

KI-BILDE: Bildet her ble delt 23. september 2024, etter at Hizbollah utfrte et rakettangrep mot Israel. Foto: X / @drhossamsamy65

22\. september 2024 ble Israel utsatt for et stort rakettangrep fra Hizbollah.

Like etterp gikk bildet ovenfor viralt som dokumentasjon p at rakettene hadde forrsaket store skader p militrbasen Ramat David i den nordlige delen av landet.

Bildet ble delt av de propalestinske profilene p X[SilencedSirs](https://x.com/SilentlySirs/status/1837936858652725379)
og[Dr. Sam Youssef](https://mobile.x.com/drhossamsamy65/status/1838022636841979974)
, og i skrivende stund er den sett over 500.000 ganger.

 Bilde fra Ramat David-basen i det okkuperte Palestina, etter at basen ble rammet av Hizbollahs angrep, skriver SilencedSirs i den medflgende teksten til innlegget.

Iflge Dr. Sam Youssef sier bildet ble lekket gjennom israelsk sensur, og iflge ham beviser det at det er omfattende skader p basen.

Men hva beviser egentlig bildet?

Zoomer du inn, er det flere mistenkelige ting ved motivet.

Flyet har en mystisk pukkel nr haleroret, lastebilen til venstre har en enorm dr, og bilen nederst har to frontender.  

  ![FEIL: Bildet er fullt av tegn p at det ble generert av kunstig intelligens. X / @drhossamsamy65 Foto: X / @drhossamsamy65](https://www.cdn.tv2.no/images/17063728.webp?imageId=17063728&x=0.00&y=0.00&cropw=100.00&croph=100.00&width=675&height=783 "Foto: X / @drhossamsamy65")

FEIL: Bildet er fullt av tegn p at det ble generert av kunstig intelligens. X / @drhossamsamy65 Foto: X / @drhossamsamy65

Samtidig er det brennende flyet av en type som ikke eksisterer i virkeligheten, og det ser ut til  vre satt sammen av et Hercules-fly og en Boeing 707.

Hvis du blar raskt forbi det falske bildet, kan det vre vanskelig  se at det er fabrikkert, og de som ser det uten  ha mistanke om det, kan tro at Israel ble hardt rammet av angrepet fra Hizbollah, selv om bildet ikke dokumenterer noe i den retningen.

Bildet av det brennende flyet tilhrer de mer sofistikerte AI-genererte bildene fra konflikten i Midtsten.

Det brukes ofte mer upraktiske lsninger, hvor gamle bilder er forkledd som nye, eller hvor bildene kommer fra helt andre steder.

 Iransk stats-TV har nettopp vist dette.

Men zoomer man inn p de mobile rampene, viser det seg at det er gamle jugoslaviske kjrety, som i dag kun brukes av Bosnia, Serbia og Kroatia.

Det har de ikke.

En mosk i brann
----------------

Noen av de fabrikkerte videoene og bildene som florerer p sosiale medier, deles ikke ndvendigvis for  lure folk, selv om de ser naturtro ut ved frste yekast.

13\. august[delte](https://x.com/TheTempleMoun/status/1823370869021831312)
for eksempel den hyreekstreme israelske gruppen Sons of the Temple Mount en video som viser den muslimske helligdommen Al Aqsa-moskeen i flammer.

[https://twitter.com/TheTempleMoun/status/1823370869021831312](https://twitter.com/TheTempleMoun/status/1823370869021831312)

 Absolutt seier, heter det i den tilhrende teksten.

Heldigvis er det et[webkamera](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=niaaMHL3Mak)
som peker direkte mot Al Aqsa-moskeen, s det er ganske enkelt  forsikre seg om at helligdommen fortsatt er der.  

Men intensjonen med den naturtro videoen, som ble laget med kunstig intelligens, var nok ogs annet enn  spre falske nyheter.

Nemlig  provosere.

Videoen har i skrivende stund kun blitt vist noen hundre ganger p gruppens egen profil p X, men til gjengjeld ble den raskt plukket opp av et stort antall palestinske profiler som raser mot den jdiske trusselen.

Videoen har blitt sett rundt 100.000 ganger p propalestinske profiler som[Eye on Palestine](https://x.com/EyeonPalestine/status/1834146323953574201)
,[DOA Muslims](https://x.com/doamuslims/status/1834198658570449027)
samt den antisionistiske kanalen[Torah Judaism](https://x.com/TorahJudaism/status/1834245765624938637)
.

Og hvis formlet med videoen var  provosere, lyktes det.

For 15. september kunne den israelske avisen[Haaretz](https://www.haaretz.com/israel-news/2024-09-15/ty-article/.premium/hamas-warns-grave-consequences-after-jewish-extremists-threaten-al-aqsa-mosque-in-video/00000191-f5e0-d570-ab95-fdedbd340000)
fortelle at den palestinske terrorbevegelsen Hamas advarte om alvorlige konsekvenser p grunn av videobildene av den brennende moskeen.  

De digitale skyene
--------------------

Ett r inn i krigen er mengden manipulert informasjon i konflikten s alvorlig at selv relativt ubetydelig informasjon n mtes med mistillit.

For eksempel etter Irans missilangrep mot Israel 1. oktober.

Her har israelerne i ettertid holdt informasjonen om hva iranerne traff tett inntil brystet.

S langt har ikke Israels militre publisert noen bilder av ml som er truffet, og pressen har ikke tilgang til de berrte basene.

Derfor ventet lenestolekspertene p internett, som flger krigen tett, lenge p at det skulle komme nye satellittbilder etter angrepene.

Men da de kom, var det en skuffelse.

[Den anonyme X-profilen Ayden](https://x.com/squatsons/status/1841548683566821424)
publiserte 2. oktoberet satellittbilde av en av de israelske basene som var mlet for det iranske angrepet, og her er det ikke mulig  se basen p grunn av skydekket.

[https://twitter.com/squatsons/status/1841548683566821424](https://twitter.com/squatsons/status/1841548683566821424)

Ayden publiserer sin egen analyse av materiale fra konfliktomrder til sine 149.000 flgere, og profilens eier konkluderte med at skyene var digitalt plassert slik at publikum ikke kan se ettervirkningene av angrepet.

I skrivende stund har den oppsiktsvekkende pstanden blitt sett 1,7 millioner ganger p Aydens profil alene.

Pstanden ble ogs umiddelbart plukket opp av en rekke propalestinske[profiler](https://x.com/ShaykhSulaiman/status/1841533871587836034)
som den britiske journalisten Sulaiman Ahmed, som delte det som et faktum med sine 598.000 flgere p X.

 Breaking. Israel legger falske digitale skyer over Nevatim-basen. De vil ikke at du skal se skadene, skrev han.

Det er imidlertid ingen indikasjoner p at satellittbildene har blitt manipulert.

Det var spredt skydekke over store deler av Israel de dagene de ble tatt.

  ![SKYDEKKE: Slik s det ut over Israel 1. oktober. Foto: Copernicus Sentinel data 2024 / TV 2 DK](https://www.cdn.tv2.no/images/17063801.webp?imageId=17063801&width=978&height=551 "Foto: Copernicus Sentinel data 2024 / TV 2 DK")

SKYDEKKE: Slik s det ut over Israel 1. oktober. Foto: Copernicus Sentinel data 2024 / TV 2 DK

P bildet med de digitale skyene kan man se en br overgang mellom bakke- og skydekke, men dette er fordi bildet er en mosaikk bygd opp av bilder fra ulike satellittpasseringer til forskjellige tider.

Pstanden om at Israel utplasserte digitale skyer for  dekke over skadene varte ikke mer enn noen f dager, og det er n offentlig tilgjengelige satellittbilder som viser skader og kratre i bakken ved den israelske basen.

Artikkelen er oppdatert

Antall visninger"

JudgePrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
**Determine the Claim's veracity** by following these steps:
1. Briefly summarize the key insights from the fact-check (see Record) in at most one paragraph.
2. Write one paragraph about which one of the Decision Options applies best. Include the most appropriate decision option at the end and enclose it in backticks like `this`.




## Decision Options
* `not enough information`: The fact-check does not contain sufficient information to come to an conclusion. For example,there is substantial lack of evidence or the evidence is inconclusive, conflicting or self-contradictory. In the case of a lack of evidence, state which information exactly is missing. In particular, if no RESULTS or sources are available, pick this decision.
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.
* `false`: The claim is not factually accurate. This is the case if one of the following three conditions is met:(1) The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources,(2) The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the origin, content and/or meaning of a statement or an image is misrepresented. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way,(3) There is not enough evidence to verify the claim or the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory.

JudgePrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
**Determine the Claim's veracity** by following these steps:
1. Briefly summarize the key insights from the fact-check (see Record) in at most one paragraph.
2. Write one paragraph about which one of the Decision Options applies best. Include the most appropriate decision option at the end and enclose it in backticks like `this`.




## Decision Options
* `not enough information`: The fact-check does not contain sufficient information to come to an conclusion. For example,there is substantial lack of evidence or the evidence is inconclusive, conflicting or self-contradictory. In the case of a lack of evidence, state which information exactly is missing. In particular, if no RESULTS or sources are available, pick this decision.
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.
* `false`: The claim is not factually accurate. This is the case if one of the following three conditions is met:(1) The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources,(2) The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the origin, content and/or meaning of a statement or an image is misrepresented. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way,(3) There is not enough evidence to verify the claim or the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory.

PlanPrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
The available knowledge is insufficient to assess the Claim. Therefore, **propose a set of actions** to retrieve new and helpful evidence. Adhere to the following rules:
* The actions available are listed under Valid Actions, including a short description for each action. No other actions are possible at this moment. 
* For each action, use the formatting as specified in Valid Actions.
* Include all actions in a single Markdown code block at the end of your answer.
* Propose as few actions as possible, but as much as needed. Do not propose similar or previously used actions.



## Valid Actions
* `geolocate`
   * Description: Performs geolocation to determine the country where an image was taken.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will determine the most likely countries where it was taken.
   * Format: geolocate(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `image_search`
   * Description: Run an image search on Google to retrieve related images for a given query.
   * How to use: This is a helpful tool for fact-checking images. Use this to retrieve images associated with a specific keyword or phrase. Ensure that the query is clear and specific to improve search accuracy. If no relevant images are found, refine the query or use more descriptive terms.
   * Format: image_search("your image search query goes here")

# Example: geolocate()

...

```

```

# Instructions

Content: Al Jazeera published a timeline of Israel's attacks on Gaza since 2005. The timeline includes military assaults in 2008-9, 2012, 2014, and 2021. <image:7789>


# Your Analysis



===== > RESPONSE:  < =====
The evidence indicates that Joan Laporta met with Isaac Herzog, the President of Israel, but the exact date is not specified. However, a Marca article featuring Joan Laporta was published on July 18, 2021. Additionally, a timeline from Al Jazeera shows military assaults on Gaza in 2021.

The claim states the meeting occurred in September 2024, which is not supported by the evidence. The evidence suggests the meeting happened before September 2024. The claim also mentions the ongoing Gaza war, which is partially supported by the timeline of attacks.

Therefore, the claim is likely false because the meeting date is incorrect.
